        <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EuropaInterior1.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Two models for the composition of Europa predict a large subsurface ocean of liquid water. Similar models have been proposed for other celestial bodies in the Solar System.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Although Earth is the only known\n       <a href="/wiki/Planet" title="Planet">\n        planet\n       </a>\n       with large stable bodies of liquid water on its surface and the only one in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Solar_System" title="Solar System">\n        Solar System\n       </a>\n       , other celestial bodies are thought to have large oceans.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-20150407_58-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NASA-20150407-58">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Planets">\n        Planets\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Gas_giant" title="Gas giant">\n        gas giants\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Jupiter" title="Jupiter">\n        Jupiter\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Saturn" title="Saturn">\n        Saturn\n       </a>\n       , are thought to lack surfaces and instead have a stratum of\n       <a href="/wiki/Liquid_hydrogen" title="Liquid hydrogen">\n        liquid hydrogen\n       </a>\n       , however their\n       <a href="/wiki/Planetary_geology" title="Planetary geology">\n        planetary geology\n       </a>\n       is not well understood. The possibility of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ice_giant" title="Ice giant">\n        ice giants\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Uranus" title="Uranus">\n        Uranus\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Neptune" title="Neptune">\n        Neptune\n       </a>\n       having hot, highly compressed,\n       <a href="/wiki/Supercritical_fluid" title="Supercritical fluid">\n        supercritical\n       </a>\n       water under their thick atmospheres has been hypothesised. Although their composition is still not fully understood, a 2006 study by Wiktorowicz and Ingersall ruled out the possibility of such a water "ocean" existing on Neptune,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WiktorowiczIngersoll2007_59-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WiktorowiczIngersoll2007-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       though some studies have suggested that exotic oceans of liquid\n       <a href="/wiki/Diamond" title="Diamond">\n        diamond\n       </a>\n       are possible.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Silvera2010_60-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Silvera2010-60">\n         [60]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars_ocean_hypothesis" title="Mars ocean hypothesis">\n        Mars ocean hypothesis\n       </a>\n       suggests that nearly a third of the surface of Mars was once covered by water, though the water on Mars is no longer oceanic (much of it residing in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Martian_polar_ice_caps" title="Martian polar ice caps">\n        ice caps\n       </a>\n       ). The possibility continues to be studied along with reasons for their apparent disappearance. Astronomers think that\n       <a href="/wiki/Atmosphere_of_Venus" title="Atmosphere of Venus">\n        Venus\n       </a>\n       had liquid water and perhaps oceans in its very early history.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2015)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       If they existed, all later vanished via\n       <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_Venus" title="Geology of Venus">\n        resurfacing\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_satellites">\n        Natural satellites\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       A global layer of liquid water thick enough to decouple the crust from the mantle is thought to be present on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Natural_satellite" title="Natural satellite">\n        natural satellites\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Titan_(moon)" title="Titan (moon)">\n        Titan\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Europa_(moon)" title="Europa (moon)">\n        Europa\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Enceladus" title="Enceladus">\n        Enceladus\n       </a>\n       and, with less certainty,\n       <a href="/wiki/Callisto_(moon)" title="Callisto (moon)">\n        Callisto\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Ganymede_(moon)" title="Ganymede (moon)">\n        Ganymede\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-clubsandwich_2014_61-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-clubsandwich_2014-61">\n         [61]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vance_62-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Vance-62">\n         [62]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Triton_(moon)" title="Triton (moon)">\n        Triton\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EncycSolSys-Triton_63-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-EncycSolSys-Triton-63">\n         [63]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ocean_triton_64-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ocean_triton-64">\n         [64]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A\n       <a href="/wiki/Magma" title="Magma">\n        magma\n       </a>\n       ocean is thought to be present on\n       <a href="/wiki/Io_(moon)" title="Io (moon)">\n        Io\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Geyser" title="Geyser">\n        Geysers\n       </a>\n       have been found on Saturn\'s moon\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Enceladus_(moon)" title="Enceladus (moon)">\n        Enceladus\n       </a>\n       , possibly originating from about 10 kilometers (6.2\xc2\xa0mi) deep ocean beneath an ice shell.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-20140403_56-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NASA-20140403-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Other\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Icy_moons" title="Icy moons">\n        icy moons\n       </a>\n       may also have internal oceans, or may once have had internal oceans that have now frozen.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hussmann_Sohl_et_al._2006_65-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Hussmann_Sohl_et_al._2006-65">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Large bodies of liquid hydrocarbons are thought to be present on the surface of\n       <a href="/wiki/Titan_(moon)" title="Titan (moon)">\n        Titan\n       </a>\n       , although they are not large enough to be considered oceans and are sometimes referred to as\n       <i>\n        lakes\n       </i>\n       or seas. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens" title="Cassini\xe2\x80\x93Huygens">\n        Cassini\xe2\x80\x93Huygens\n       </a>\n       space mission initially discovered only what appeared to be dry lakebeds and empty river channels, suggesting that Titan had lost what surface liquids it might have had. Cassini\'s more recent fly-by of Titan offers radar images that strongly suggest hydrocarbon lakes exist near the colder polar regions. Titan is thought to have a subsurface liquid-water ocean under the ice and hydrocarbon mix that forms its outer crust.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Dwarf_planets_and_trans-Neptunian_objects">\n        Dwarf planets and trans-Neptunian objects\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ceres_Cutaway-en.svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="963" data-file-width="1200" height="177" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Ceres_Cutaway-en.svg/220px-Ceres_Cutaway-en.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Ceres_Cutaway-en.svg/330px-Ceres_Cutaway-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Ceres_Cutaway-en.svg/440px-Ceres_Cutaway-en.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ceres_Cutaway-en.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Diagram showing a possible internal structure of\n         <a href="/wiki/Ceres_(dwarf_planet)" title="Ceres (dwarf planet)">\n          Ceres\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Ceres_(dwarf_planet)" title="Ceres (dwarf planet)">\n        Ceres\n       </a>\n       appears to be\n       <a href="/wiki/Planetary_differentiation" title="Planetary differentiation">\n        differentiated\n       </a>\n       into a\n       <a href="/wiki/Rock_(geology)" title="Rock (geology)">\n        rocky\n       </a>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Core_(geology)" title="Core (geology)">\n        core\n       </a>\n       and icy\n       <a href="/wiki/Mantle_(geology)" title="Mantle (geology)">\n        mantle\n       </a>\n       and may harbour a liquid-water ocean under its surface.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mccord.2005_66-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-mccord.2005-66">\n         [66]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cr.ceres_67-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-cr.ceres-67">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Not enough is known of the larger\n       <a href="/wiki/Trans-Neptunian_object" title="Trans-Neptunian object">\n        trans-Neptunian objects\n       </a>\n       to determine whether they are differentiated bodies capable of supporting oceans, although models of radioactive decay suggest that\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pluto_(dwarf_planet)" title="Pluto (dwarf planet)">\n        Pluto\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pluto_68-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-pluto-68">\n         [68]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Eris_(dwarf_planet)" title="Eris (dwarf planet)">\n        Eris\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/90377_Sedna" title="90377 Sedna">\n        Sedna\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/90482_Orcus" title="90482 Orcus">\n        Orcus\n       </a>\n       have oceans beneath solid icy crusts approximately\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        100 to 180 km\n       </span>\n       thick.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hussmann_Sohl_et_al._2006_65-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Hussmann_Sohl_et_al._2006-65">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Extrasolar">\n        Extrasolar\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UpsilonAndromedae_D_moons.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="474" data-file-width="735" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/UpsilonAndromedae_D_moons.jpg/220px-UpsilonAndromedae_D_moons.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/UpsilonAndromedae_D_moons.jpg/330px-UpsilonAndromedae_D_moons.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/UpsilonAndromedae_D_moons.jpg/440px-UpsilonAndromedae_D_moons.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UpsilonAndromedae_D_moons.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Rendering of a hypothetical large\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extrasolar_moon" title="Extrasolar moon">\n          extrasolar moon\n         </a>\n         with surface liquid-water oceans\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Some planets and natural satellites outside the Solar System are likely to have oceans, including possible water ocean planets similar to Earth in the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Habitable_zone" title="Habitable zone">\n        habitable zone\n       </a>\n       or "liquid-water belt". The detection of oceans, even through the\n       <a href="/wiki/Spectroscopy" title="Spectroscopy">\n        spectroscopy\n       </a>\n       method, however is likely extremely difficult and inconclusive.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Theoretical models have been used to predict with high probability that\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GJ_1214_b" title="GJ 1214 b">\n        GJ 1214 b\n       </a>\n       , detected by transit, is composed of exotic form of\n       <a href="/wiki/Ice_VII" title="Ice VII">\n        ice VII\n       </a>\n       , making up 75% of its mass,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cfa.pr200924_69-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-cfa.pr200924-69">\n         [69]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       making it an\n       <a href="/wiki/Ocean_planet" title="Ocean planet">\n        ocean planet\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Other possible candidates are merely speculated based on their mass and position in the habitable zone include planet though little is actually known of their composition. Some scientists speculate\n       <a href="/wiki/Kepler-22b" title="Kepler-22b">\n        Kepler-22b\n       </a>\n       may be an "ocean-like" planet.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-upr.exo_70-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-upr.exo-70">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Models have been proposed for\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gliese_581_d" title="Gliese 581 d">\n        Gliese 581 d\n       </a>\n       that could include surface oceans.\n       <a href="/wiki/Gliese_436_b" title="Gliese 436 b">\n        Gliese 436 b\n       </a>\n       is speculated to have an ocean of "hot ice".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-r.20070516_71-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-r.20070516-71">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Exomoon" title="Exomoon">\n        Exomoons\n       </a>\n       orbiting planets, particularly gas giants within their parent star\'s habitable zone may theoretically have surface oceans.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Terrestrial planets will acquire water during their accretion, some of which will be buried in the magma ocean but most of it will go into a steam atmosphere, and when the atmosphere cools it will collapse on to the surface forming an ocean. There will also be outgassing of water from the mantle as the magma solidifies\xe2\x80\x94this will happen even for planets with a low percentage of their mass composed of water, so "super-Earth exoplanets may be expected to commonly produce water oceans within tens to hundreds of millions of years of their last major accretionary impact."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ass.332_72-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ass.332-72">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Non-water_surface_liquids">\n        Non-water surface liquids\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Oceans, seas, lakes and other bodies of liquids can be composed of liquids other than water, for example the\n       <a href="/wiki/Hydrocarbon" title="Hydrocarbon">\n        hydrocarbon\n       </a>\n       lakes on\n       <a href="/wiki/Titan_(moon)" title="Titan (moon)">\n        Titan\n       </a>\n       . The possibility of seas of\n       <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen" title="Nitrogen">\n        nitrogen\n       </a>\n       on\n       <a href="/wiki/Triton_(moon)" title="Triton (moon)">\n        Triton\n       </a>\n       was also considered but ruled out.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-encyc_73-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-encyc-73">\n         [73]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       There is evidence that the icy surfaces of the moons\n       <a href="/wiki/Ganymede_(moon)" title="Ganymede (moon)">\n        Ganymede\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Callisto_(moon)" title="Callisto (moon)">\n        Callisto\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Europa_(moon)" title="Europa (moon)">\n        Europa\n       </a>\n       , Titan and\n       <a href="/wiki/Enceladus" title="Enceladus">\n        Enceladus\n       </a>\n       are shells floating on oceans of very dense liquid water or water\xe2\x80\x93ammonia.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-agu.p21a_74-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-agu.p21a-74">\n         [74]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ic.208_75-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ic.208-75">\n         [75]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ar.0032_76-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ar.0032-76">\n         [76]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cop.213_77-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-cop.213-77">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ucsc.2008_78-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ucsc.2008-78">\n         [78]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Earth is often called\n       <i>\n        the\n       </i>\n       ocean planet because it is 70% covered in water.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nih.12349465_79-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nih.12349465-79">\n         [79]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sci.1998_80-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sci.1998-80">\n         [80]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Extrasolar\n       <a href="/wiki/Terrestrial_planet" title="Terrestrial planet">\n        terrestrial planets\n       </a>\n       that are extremely close to their parent star will be tidally locked and so one half of the planet will be a magma ocean.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ar.1204_81-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ar.1204-81">\n         [81]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It is also possible that terrestrial planets had magma oceans at some point during their formation as a result of giant impacts.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nmsu.oem_82-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nmsu.oem-82">\n         [82]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Hot_Neptune" title="Hot Neptune">\n        Hot Neptunes\n       </a>\n       close to their star could lose their atmospheres via\n       <a href="/wiki/Hydrodynamic_escape" title="Hydrodynamic escape">\n        hydrodynamic escape\n       </a>\n       , leaving behind their cores with various liquids on the surface.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-epsc.542_83-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-epsc.542-83">\n         [83]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Where there are suitable temperatures and pressures, volatile chemicals that might exist as liquids in abundant quantities on planets include\n       <a href="/wiki/Ammonia" title="Ammonia">\n        ammonia\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Argon" title="Argon">\n        argon\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Carbon_disulfide" title="Carbon disulfide">\n        carbon disulfide\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Ethane" title="Ethane">\n        ethane\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Hydrazine" title="Hydrazine">\n        hydrazine\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen" title="Hydrogen">\n        hydrogen\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_cyanide" title="Hydrogen cyanide">\n        hydrogen cyanide\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_sulfide" title="Hydrogen sulfide">\n        hydrogen sulfide\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Methane" title="Methane">\n        methane\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Neon" title="Neon">\n        neon\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen" title="Nitrogen">\n        nitrogen\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Nitric_oxide" title="Nitric oxide">\n        nitric oxide\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Phosphine" title="Phosphine">\n        phosphine\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Silane" title="Silane">\n        silane\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Sulfuric_acid" title="Sulfuric acid">\n        sulfuric acid\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Water" title="Water">\n        water\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ifa.a281_84-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ifa.a281-84">\n         [84]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Supercritical fluids, although not liquids, do share various properties with liquids. Underneath the thick atmospheres of the planets\n       <a href="/wiki/Uranus" title="Uranus">\n        Uranus\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Neptune" title="Neptune">\n        Neptune\n       </a>\n       , it is expected that these planets are composed of oceans of hot high-density fluid mixtures of water, ammonia and other volatiles.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cosis.05179_85-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-cosis.05179-85">\n         [85]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The gaseous outer layers of\n       <a href="/wiki/Jupiter" title="Jupiter">\n        Jupiter\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Saturn" title="Saturn">\n        Saturn\n       </a>\n       transition smoothly into oceans of\n       <a href="/wiki/Supercritical_fluid" title="Supercritical fluid">\n        supercritical\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen" title="Hydrogen">\n        hydrogen\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pss.1999_86-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-pss.1999-86">\n         [86]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lang03_87-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-lang03-87">\n         [87]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Atmosphere_of_Venus" title="Atmosphere of Venus">\n        atmosphere of Venus\n       </a>\n       is 96.5%\n       <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">\n        carbon dioxide\n       </a>\n       , which is a supercritical fluid at its surface.\n      </p>\n
